The Word 'Ay' and the Precedence of Existence
Commentator clarifies precedence is of existence, and temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the commentator specifies that precedence in temporal origination belongs to existence rather than essence, and why this precedence is temporal.

Core Idea
Temporal origination attaches to existence, not essence.

In this short passage from the commentary, the scholar clarifies a subtle but crucial point in the definition of temporal origination (al-haduth). The phrase 'preceded by non-existence' could be misunderstood as referring to the essence itself. The commentator corrects this, showing that it is existence that is preceded, and that this precedence is temporal. This lesson unpacks that clarification and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text aloud or silently. Then read the literal translation to grasp the basic meaning. Notice how the commentator uses the word 'ay' to signal an explanation.
2
Identify the two clarifications
The passage makes two distinct points: (1) precedence relates to existence, not essence, and (2) the precedence is temporal. Locate each in the text.
3
Consider the common misunderstanding
The commentary addresses the misconception that the essence itself is preceded by non-existence. Reflect on why this distinction matters for understanding divine attributes.
4
Apply the lesson
Now that you know that al-haduth is an attribute of existence, think about how this affects the way we speak about created things and their relation to time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أي) يكون إلخ ) إِشارة إلى أن المراد مسبوقية وجوده، إذ لا مسبوقية للذات عن العدم، فالحدوث صفة للوجود في نفسه وللحادث باعتبار متعلقه وإلى أن المراد المسبوقية الزمانية، إذ قبلية العدم على الوجود زمانية .
His saying: (meaning) etc. is an indication that what is intended is the precedence of its existence, because there is no precedence of the essence over non-existence. Thus, origination is an attribute of existence itself, and of the originated thing with respect to its attribute. And it is an indication that what is intended is temporal precedence, because the priority of non-existence over existence is temporal.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage explains the word 'ay' (meaning) in the first definition. The commentator clarifies that the intended meaning of 'preceded by non-existence' is the precedence of its existence, not the essence. The essence itself is not preceded by non-existence; rather, it is the existence that has non-existence before it. Therefore, origination (al-haduth) is an attribute of existence itself, and it is attributed to the originated thing (al-hadith) by virtue of its attribute (existence). Furthermore, this precedence is temporal, because the priority of non-existence over existence is a temporal priority. This distinguishes temporal origination from essential origination.

Key Terms
أي
مسبوقية
وجود
ذات
الحدوث
صفة للوجود
المسبوقية الزمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the essence itself is preceded by non-existence.
Correction: The commentator stresses that it is existence that is preceded, not the essence.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator say about the precedence in the definition of temporal origination?
A) It is the precedence of the essence over non-existence.
B) It is the precedence of existence, and it is temporal.
C) It is the precedence of the originated thing over its cause.
D) It is the precedence of non-existence over the essence.

Key Takeaway
Temporal origination is an attribute of existence, not essence, and its precedence over non-existence is temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The commentator states that origination is an attribute of existence, not of your essence. What does your essence rely on for its sense of permanence? Is it your existence, or something beyond it? If your essence is not defined by temporal existence, how does that reframe your identity in relation to the Eternal?
?
Temporal origination means your existence is a gift that came from non-existence. Have you truly absorbed that there was a time when you were not, and that your very being is a creative act sustained moment by moment? What would change in your daily gratitude and reliance if you lived with this awareness every moment?
?
The passage emphasizes that non-existence precedes existence temporally. Are you living as though your existence is a fleeting moment between two eternities? Or do you act as if you will always be here? What specific decision today will reflect the truth that you are originated and dependent on the Eternal?

Essential Precedence and the Generality of Origination
Commentator explains the logical distinction between essential and temporal precedence in defining the originated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why essential precedence makes the concept of 'originated' more general in existence (wujudan) but not in truth (sidqan), and how this refines the definitions of eternal and originated.

Core Idea
Essential precedence broadens the scope of origination existentially, not truthfully.

This passage delves into a subtle point about the second definition of the originated. The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'essential precedence' is used intentionally to make the originated more general in a specific way. Understanding this distinction between existential and truthful generality is crucial for grasping the precise boundaries of the concepts of eternal and originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Focus on the context of inference (qarinat al-tafri') and the logical reasoning.
Note the key terms: سبق ذاتي, الحدوث الذاتي, الحدوث الزماني.
2
Identify the two kinds of generality
The commentator distinguishes between being more general in truth (sidqan) and in existence (wujudan). Notice that essential origination is more general only existentially.
This means essential origination applies to more entities, but does not change the truth conditions of what it means to be originated.
3
Understand the counterfactual
Consider what would happen if temporal precedence were intended: essential and temporal originated would be equal, and similarly the two eternals would be limited. This shows why essential precedence is needed.
The equality would collapse the distinction between types of originated things.
4
Analyze the author's phrasing
The author says 'whether there is temporal precedence or not' rather than 'whether temporal or not'. This subtle wording indicates the broader existential scope.
The phrase 'or not' extends the application to cases without temporal precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (سبقاً ذاتياً ) بقرينة التفريع أعني قوله : فيكون الحادث أعم فإنه لو أريد السبق الزماني كان الحادث الذاتي والزماني متساويين وكذا القديمان ضرورة أن المسبوق بالغير سبقاً زمانيا يكون ذلك الغير في زمان عدمه وإنما لم يرد الأعم من الذاتي والزماني لأن الحدوث الذاتي ليس أعم من الحدوث الزماني صدقاً بل وجوداً يشير إليه قوله سواء كان هناك سبق زماني أو لا حيث لم يقل سواء كان زمانيا أو لا.
His saying: (essential precedence) due to the context of inference, namely his saying: 'so that the originated would be more general', because if temporal precedence were intended, the essential and temporal originated would be equal, and similarly the two eternals, necessarily, because that which is preceded by another temporally has that other in the time of its non-existence. And he did not intend the more general of essential and temporal, because essential origination is not more general than temporal origination in terms of truth, but in terms of existence. This is indicated by his saying: 'whether there is temporal precedence or not', where he did not say 'whether it is temporal or not'.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase 'essential precedence' (sabq dhati) used in the second definition. The commentator points to the context of inference (qarinat al-tafri'), namely the author's statement that the originated would be more general (fayakun al-hadith a'am). If temporal precedence were intended, then the essential and temporal originated would be coextensive, and similarly the eternal would be limited. But the author's phrase 'whether there is temporal precedence or not' shows that essential precedence is broader in existence (wujudan) not in truth (sidqan). That is, essential origination applies in more situations, but does not change the truth conditions. The commentator clarifies that the author deliberately said 'whether there is temporal precedence or not' instead of 'whether temporal or not' to indicate the broader existential scope.

Key Terms
سبق ذاتي
الحادث أعم
الحدوث الذاتي
الحدوث الزماني
صدقاً
وجوداً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some students think essential origination is a broader concept than temporal origination in terms of truth (sidqan), i.e., that more things satisfy the definition of 'essential originated' than 'temporal originated'.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that essential origination is not more general in truth; it is more general in existence (wujudan). That is, it applies to a wider range of existing entities, but the truth conditions for calling something 'originated' are the same for both types.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is essential origination said to be more general?
A) In terms of truth (sidqan), it includes more cases.
B) In terms of existence (wujudan), it applies to more entities.
C) It is actually less general than temporal origination.
D) Because it includes both temporal and atemporal precedence.

Key Takeaway
Essential precedence makes the originated more general existentially, allowing it to include both temporal and atemporal originated entities, while the truthful definition remains unchanged.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you think of your own existence as being essentially dependent on Allah at every moment, not just at the beginning of your life? Does this change how you approach your daily routine? What one action can you take today to live in constant awareness of that dependency?
?
This lesson shows that even your thoughts and mental concepts are 'originated' in the essential sense—they depend on Allah for their existence. Are there thoughts or beliefs you hold that you unconsciously treat as independent or self-sufficient? How can you submit even your inner world to Allah's sovereignty?
?
The commentator warns against confusing a broader existential application with a truth claim. In your own life, where might you be mistaking something that is merely 'more common' or 'more widespread' for something that is true? What would it cost you to align your life with truth rather than with what is merely existentially general?

The Generalization in the Second Definition
Commentator clarifies the generalization's effect on the second definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the generalization in the second definition of 'originated' broadens its scope from non-existence precedence to any other precedence.

Core Idea
The second definition is not limited to non-existence precedence.

The commentator clarifies that the phrase "whether there is temporal precedence or not" serves as a generalization. It indicates that the second definition of the originated—that which is preceded by another—is not restricted to cases where the precedence is that of non-existence. Instead, it includes other forms of precedence, such as essential precedence. This nuance ensures that the definition is comprehensive without negating the first definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the commentator's words stand before you interpret.
Notice the key term 'تعميم' (generalization).
2
Identify the generalization
The phrase 'whether there is temporal precedence or not' is the generalization. Find it in the Arabic text.
It is indicated by 'سواء كان إلخ'.
3
Understand the implication
The generalization means that the second definition ('the originated is that which is preceded by another') is not limited to being preceded by non-existence. It includes other types of precedence.
This broadens the definition.
4
Clarify the common misunderstanding
Some might think this generalization cancels the first definition. But the commentator says it only expands the scope, not negates the first definition.
The first definition remains valid as a specific case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( سواء كان إلخ) أشار بهذا التعميم إلى أن حصر الحادث على المسبوق بالغير معناه أنه ليس مقصوراً على المسبوق بالعدم لا على أنه ليس ذلك معناه .
His saying: (whether there is etc.) He indicated by this generalization that restricting the originated to that which is preceded by another means that it is not limited to that which is preceded by non-existence, not that it is not its meaning.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This short passage comments on the phrase 'whether there is temporal precedence or not' (sawa'a kana hunalika sabq zamani aw la). The commentator says that by this generalization, the author indicates that the second definition—'the originated is that which is preceded by another'—is not limited to being preceded by non-existence. In other words, the second definition includes cases of essential precedence as well. The commentator stresses that this does not negate the meaning of the first definition; it simply expands the scope. The first definition remains correct as a specific type of origination (temporal), but the second definition is more general.

Key Terms

مسبوق بالغير
مسبوق بالعدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The generalization cancels the first definition (being preceded by non-existence).
Correction: The generalization only shows that the second definition is not restricted to non-existence precedence; the first definition remains valid as a specific case.

Checkpoint
What does the generalization 'whether there is temporal precedence or not' indicate?
A) That the originated is only that which is preceded by non-existence.
B) That the second definition is not limited to being preceded by non-existence.
C) That temporal precedence is the only kind of precedence.
D) That the first definition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The generalization shows that the second definition of the originated is not limited to non-existence precedence, but includes other forms of precedence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider your own spiritual journey. Are there ways you have been using a too-limited definition of what it means to be 'created' or 'dependent'? This lesson invites you to broaden that definition. What aspect of your life is 'preceded by another' in a non-temporal sense—like your reliance on Allah for existence moment by moment? How can you make that awareness more immediate in your daily consciousness?
?
The commentator emphasizes that the first definition (preceded by non-existence) is not cancelled. In your own understanding of faith, do you sometimes feel that a broader perspective cancels the simpler truths? How can you hold both the specific and the general without dismissing one? Give a concrete example from your practice of Islam.
?
This passage is a subtle logical point. In your pursuit of Islamic knowledge, do you sometimes dismiss such fine distinctions as 'too academic'? Yet the commentator takes great care to clarify. How might your spiritual life change if you approached theological distinctions with the same precision and reverence? What one small step can you take this week to delve deeper into a nuanced point of aqeedah?

Philosophers' Proof for Essential Origination
Presents the philosophers' argument for essential origination and the commentator's critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' argument for essential origination and the commentator's critique of its logical basis.

Core Idea
Essential origination means non-existence is prior to existence in essence, not in time.

This passage presents the key proof used by philosophers to establish that the contingent world is originated in essence. The commentator guides us through the logic, explains the terminology, and then raises a serious problem with the argument. Understanding this discussion is crucial for grasping the Islamic critique of philosophical cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation. Notice the structure: first the proof, then the commentator's remarks.
The passage includes both the philosophers' statement and the commentator's clarifications.
2
Identify the three premises
The proof has two explicit premises and a reasoning that connects them. Find the statement about the contingent and the principle that what is by essence precedes what is by other.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that non-existence is prior in essence to existence for the contingent. This is called essential origination. Compare it to temporal origination.
Note the difference in mode of priority.
4
Examine the commentator's critique
The commentator says this is 'very problematic' because non-existence has no positive reality to be prior. Reflect on why this is a strong objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحكماء في إثبات الحدوث الذاتي ( الممكن لذاته غير مقتض للوجود ولغيره مقتض له وما بالذات مقدم بالذات على ما بالغير)؛ لأن ارتفاع حال الشيء ذاته يستلزم ارتفاع ذاته، وذلك يستلزم ارتفاع ما للذات بحسب الغير، وأما ارتفاع حاله بحسب غيره، فلا يقتضي ارتفاع حاله بحسب ذاته، فيتقدم ما بالذات على ما بالغير تقدم الواحد على الاثنين ( فإذن لا وجوده ) أي عدمه (مقدم على وجوده ) تقدماً (بالذات وهو أعني تقدم العدم على الوجود بالذات هو ( الحدوث الذاتي ) . ويظهر من هذا الكلام أن الحدوث الذاتي عندهم هو مسبوقية الوجود بالعدم أيضا كالحدوث الزماني، إلا أن السبق في الذاتي بالذات، وفي الزماني بالزمان، وقد صرح بذلك بعض الفضلاء، لكنه مشكل جداً. فإن العدم لا قوله : ( لذاته) متعلق بقوله : غير مقتض لا بالممكن يرشدك إلى ذلك قوله : ولغيره مقتض له . قوله : ( تقدم الواحد إلخ) أي بالطبع لا بالعلية، لعدم كفاية ارتفاع ما بالذات، بل لا بد من ارتفاع الذات أيضاً . قوله : ( ويظهر من هذا (الكلام أي من التفريع المذكور، أو من استدلالهم المذكور، فإن مسبوقية الحادث بالغير لاحتياجه إلى العلة بديهي لا يحتاج إلى الاستدلال . قوله : ( لكنه مشكل جداً قد يقال : في دفع الإشكال : إن المراد من قوله : فإذن لا اقتضاؤه قوله : (إذ المعلول القديم إن ثبت لا شبهة في ثبوته، أما عند الحكماء فظاهر، وأما عندنا فبالنظر إلى الصفات، لكن لما لم يقولوا بكونها غير الذات لم يلتفت إليه، فأورد كلمة إن الدالة على الشك. قوله : ( الممكن لذاته غير مقتض للوجود قوله : لذاته متعلق بعدم الاقتضاء، لا بالممكن كما يدل عليه قوله : ولغيره مقتض له . قوله : (وما بالذات مقدم على ما (بالغير قيل لأن ما يثبت بلا واسطة مقدم على ما يثبت بها، ولا حاجة إلى البيان المذكور، فلا يرد ما سيورده وفيه بحث؛ لأن تقدم ما بالذات على ما بالواسطة إنما يلزم إذا احتاج الثابت بالواسطة إلى الثابت بدونها، وهو ممنوع .
The philosophers said, in proving essential origination: (The contingent in itself is not necessitating of existence, but from another it is necessitating of it; and what is by essence is prior in essence to what is by other); because the removal of the state of a thing by its essence entails the removal of its essence, and that entails the removal of what is by essence in relation to the other; but the removal of its state in relation to the other does not entail the removal of its state in relation to its essence. So what is by essence is prior to what is by other with the priority of the one over the two. (Therefore, its non-existence — i.e., its non-being — is prior to its existence with an essential priority; and it — i.e., the priority of non-existence over existence in essence — is essential origination.) And it appears from this statement that essential origination according to them is also the priority of existence by non-existence, like temporal origination, except that the precedence in essential is by essence, and in temporal is by time; and some virtuous persons have explicitly stated that, but it is very problematic. For non-existence does not... His saying: (in itself) is attached to his saying: 'not necessitating', not to 'the contingent'; that is indicated by his saying: 'and from another it is necessitating of it'. His saying: (the priority of the one etc.) meaning by nature, not by causality, because removal of what is by essence is insufficient; rather, removal of the essence itself is also necessary. His saying: (And it appears from this speech) meaning from the aforementioned reasoning, or from their aforementioned argument; for the priority of the originated by another due to its need for a cause is self-evident and does not require argument. His saying: (but it is very problematic) It may be said, in refuting the problem: The intent of his saying: 'therefore, its non-existence...' is not... His saying: (For the eternal effect, if it is established) — there is no doubt about its establishment; as for the philosophers, it is evident; as for us, with respect to the attributes, but because they did not hold them to be other than the essence, he did not pay attention to it, so he used the word 'if' indicating doubt. His saying: (The contingent in itself is not necessitating of existence) — his saying 'in itself' is attached to the negation of necessitation, not to 'the contingent', as his saying 'and from another it is necessitating of it' indicates. His saying: (And what is by essence is prior to what is by other) — it is said because what is established without intermediary is prior to what is established through it, and there is no need for the mentioned explanation; so what he will raise does not apply, and there is discussion about it: because the priority of what is by essence over what is by intermediary is only necessary if the thing established through the intermediary needs the thing established without it, which is denied.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' (al-ḥukamā') proof for essential origination (al-ḥudūth al-dhātī) and the commentator's critical remarks. The argument begins with the nature of the contingent (al-mumkin): the contingent in itself is not necessitating of existence (ghayr muqtaḍin li'l-wujūd), but from another (i.e., its cause) it is necessitating of it. Then a metaphysical principle is introduced: what is by essence (mā bi'l-dhāt) is prior in essence to what is by other (mā bi'l-ghayr). The reasoning is: if the state of a thing by its essence is removed, the essence itself must be removed; and if the essence is removed, then what is by essence in relation to the other is also removed. However, removing the state by other does not require removing the state by self. Therefore, what is by essence is prior to what is by other, with a priority like that of the one over the two (i.e., natural priority). Consequently, the non-existence (i.e., the non-being) of the contingent is prior in essence to its existence. This essential priority of non-existence over existence is what they call essential origination. The commentator then notes that essential origination also involves non-existence preceding existence, like temporal origination, but the mode of precedence differs: in essential it is by essence, in temporal by time. He reports that some virtuous persons explicitly state this, but he finds it very problematic (mushkil jiddan) because non-existence does not have a positive nature to be prior. The commentary that follows explains the wording of the proof: 'in itself' modifies 'not necessitating' not 'the contingent'; 'priority of the one over the two' means natural priority, not causal; the apparent understanding from the proof is that the priority of the originated by another is self-evident and needs no proof. The commentator also addresses the problem of eternal effects (like attributes) and the statement 'if it is established' showing doubt. He ends with a discussion on the priority of what is by essence over what is by intermediary, stating that it is not universally accepted.

Key Terms
الحدوث الذاتي
الممكن
ما بالذات
ما بالغير
تقدم بالذات
العدم
العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Essential origination means that the contingent has no connection to non-existence at all.
Correction: The philosophers' essential origination still involves non-existence preceding existence, but the priority is essential (dhātī) rather than temporal.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' proof, why does non-existence precede existence in essence for the contingent?
A) Because non-existence is the original state
B) Because what is by essence is prior to what is by other
C) Because time is cyclical
D) Because the cause precedes the effect in time

Key Takeaway
Essential origination is the essential priority of non-existence over existence for the contingent, a notion the commentator finds problematic due to the non-real nature of non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are contingent: in yourself, you have no necessity to exist. If you truly internalized that your existence is not from yourself, how would your daily fears and ambitions change? What one concrete action can you take today to live with more awareness of your complete dependence on the Creator?
?
The philosophers argue that non-existence is prior in essence to your existence. Does this thought humble you, or does it create anxiety? Identify one specific thing you rely on as if it were the source of your existence (e.g., wealth, status, relationships). Then reread the passage: 'the contingent in itself is not necessitating of existence, but from another it is necessitating of it.' Commit to redirecting that reliance to God alone.
?
Reflect on the commentator's concern: non-existence is not a real thing, so how can it be 'prior'? If non-existence has no reality, what does that imply about the ultimate source of your existence? How does this deepen your conviction that God alone is truly existent and self-sufficient, and how should that conviction reshape your worship today?

The Philosophers' Proof for Essential Origination
Philosophers' rational argument for essential priority of non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' rational argument that a contingent being's non-existence is essentially prior to its existence, which they call essential origination.

Core Idea
A contingent's non-existence belongs to it by essence; existence comes from another and is therefore secondary.

The philosophers argue that origination is not merely temporal but essential—that is, non-existence is logically prior to existence. In this passage, they lay out a precise proof based on the distinction between what belongs to a thing by itself and what it receives from a cause. This argument is foundational to understanding the philosophical concept of contingency and the necessity of a creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation to get the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the key premise
Notice the opening: a contingent does not necessitate existence by itself (by essence), but does so by another (its cause). This sets up the central distinction.
3
Understand the principle of priority
The proof introduces a principle: what is by essence is essentially prior to what is by another. Follow the justification given: removing the essence removes everything, but removing what is by another does not remove the essence.
4
Apply the principle to the contingent
See how the principle is applied: non-existence is by essence, existence is by another, so non-existence is prior. This is the definition of essential origination.
5
Review the logical structure
Use the guided breakdown and learning flow to trace the proof step by step. Then test your understanding with the checkpoint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحكماء في إثبات الحدوث الذاتي: الممكن لذاته غير مقتض للوجود ولغيره مقتض له، وما بالذات مقدم بالذات على ما بالغير؛ لأن ارتفاع حال الشيء بالذات يستلزم ارتفاع ذاته، وذلك يستلزم ارتفاع ما للذات بحسب الغير، وأما ارتفاع حاله بحسب غيره فلا يقتضي ارتفاع حاله بحسب ذاته. فيتقدم ما بالذات على ما بالغير تقدم الواحد على الاثنين. فإذن لا وجوده (أي عدمه) مقدم على وجوده تقدماً بالذات، وهو أعني تقدم العدم على الوجود بالذات هو الحدوث الذاتي.
The philosophers said in proving essential origination: The contingent by essence is not necessitating of existence, but by another it is necessitating of it. And what is by essence is prior in essence to what is by another; because the elimination of a state of a thing by essence necessitates the elimination of its essence, and that necessitates the elimination of what is for the essence by another. But the elimination of its state by its other does not necessitate the elimination of its state by its essence. Thus what is by essence is prior to what is by another, like the priority of one over two. Therefore, its non-existence (i.e., its absence) is prior to its existence by essential priority, and this—namely the priority of non-existence over existence in essence—is essential origination.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' proof for essential origination. It begins by stating that a contingent being (al-mumkin) in itself does not necessitate existence; rather, it receives existence from another (its cause). Then it introduces a key principle: what belongs to a thing by essence (ma bi al-dhat) is essentially prior to what belongs to it by another (ma bi al-ghayr). The proof justifies this principle: if the state that is by essence is removed, the essence itself is removed; consequently, the state that is by another is also removed. However, removing the state that is by another does not affect the state by essence. Therefore, the state by essence is prior. Applying this: non-existence belongs to the contingent by essence (since it does not necessitate existence), while existence belongs to it by another (from the cause). Hence, non-existence is essentially prior to existence. This priority of non-existence over existence in essence is what they call essential origination.

Key Terms
الممكن (al-mumkin)
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida')
ما بالذات (ma bi al-dhat)
ما بالغير (ma bi al-ghayr)
السبق بالذات (al-sabq bi al-dhat)
العدم (al-'adam)
الوجود (al-wujud)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the philosophers' proof for origination requires temporal priority, i.e., that the contingent must have existed after not existing in time.
Correction: The proof demonstrates only essential priority (al-sabq bi al-dhāt), not temporal priority. Non-existence is logically prior in the essence of the contingent, regardless of time. Essential origination is about the dependence of existence on a cause, not about a temporal beginning.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' proof, why is non-existence essentially prior to existence for a contingent being?
A) Because contingent beings begin in time.
B) Because non-existence is its state by essence, and existence is by another, and what is by essence is prior.
C) Because existence necessarily leads to non-existence.
D) Because the cause of existence is non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Essential origination means that for a contingent being, non-existence is logically prior to existence because non-existence belongs to its essence while existence is received from a cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If non-existence is more essential to you than existence, what does that say about your claim to independence? Do you truly live as if your existence is borrowed every moment from Allah?
?
The philosophers say your existence comes from another. When you feel self-sufficient in your skills, wealth, or relationships, do you realize that even those are given by another? How can you train yourself to see your entire existence as a gift?
?
This argument proves that you are originated in your essence — you never 'deserve' existence by yourself. What would change in your prayers and your heart if you fully believed that your nonexistence is more fitting for you than your existence? How would you express gratitude?

Objection and Imam al-Razi's Refinement
Objection to philosophers' proof and al-Razi's refined definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection to the philosophers' definition of essential origination as existence preceded by non-existence, and Imam al-Razi's corrected formulation based on the priority of non-deservingness over deservingness.

Core Idea
Essential origination is not about non-existence preceding existence, but about dependence on a cause.

The philosophers define essential origination as existence preceded by non-existence in essence, not time. However, this leads to a contradiction: non-existence cannot be essentially prior to existence without being its cause. Imam al-Razi offers a refined definition: essential origination is the priority of the state of not deserving existence over deserving it, which avoids the problem. This lesson unpacks that objection and solution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the shift from describing the philosophers' view to raising an objection.
2
Identify the philosophers' claim and the objection
The passage begins by explaining that essential origination also involves priority of existence over non-existence, just like temporal origination, but by essence. The objection states that non-existence cannot be essentially prior to existence because that would make it a cause.
Focus on the phrase 'فإن العدم لا تقدم له بالذات على الوجود'.
3
Understand the objection's reasoning
If non-existence were essentially prior, it would be a cause or part of a cause of existence. This is impossible for eternally existing contingent beings like the celestial spheres.
The passage mentions 'الممكنات المستمرة الوجود في الأزل'.
4
See Imam al-Razi's alternative
The passage concludes that if we define essential origination as the priority of the state of not deserving existence over deserving it (i.e., being needful), then the definition is correct. This is al-Razi's solution.
Note the contrast: it's not about non-existence before existence, but about dependence on a cause.
5
Reflect on the significance
This distinction avoids the problematic implication that non-existence is a cause of existence. It preserves the necessity of a cause for contingent beings without that issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويظهر من هذا الكلام أن الحدوث الذاتي عندهم هو مسبوقية الوجود بالعدم أيضا كالحدوث الزماني، إلا أن السبق في الذاتي بالذات، وفي الزماني بالزمان، وقد صرح بذلك بعض الفضلاء، لكنه مشكل جداً. فإن العدم لا تقدم له بالذات على الوجود، وإلا لكان علة له أو جزءاً لعلته، ولا يتصور ذلك في الممكنات المستمرة الوجود في الأزل عندهم مع كونها محدثة حدوثاً ذاتياً. ويرد عليه أن عدم اقتضاء الوجود وإن كان أمراً ثابتاً للممكن بحسب ذاته، لكنه لا يوجب اقتضاءه العدم، فيكون عدمه سابقاً على وجوده سبقاً ذاتياً، كما زعموا. نعم لا اقتضاء الوجود والعدم لكونه مستنداً إلى ذات الممكن سابق على اقتضاء الوجود لكونه مستنداً إلى غيره، فإن جعل مسبوقية استحقاق الوجود بلا استحقاقيته حدوثاً ذاتياً، كما فعله الإمام الرازي صح.
And it appears from this statement that essential origination according to them is also the priority of existence over non-existence like temporal origination, except that the priority in essential is by essence, and in temporal is by time. And some scholars stated that explicitly, but it is very problematic. For non-existence has no essential priority over existence; otherwise it would be a cause of it or a part of its cause, and that is inconceivable for contingent beings that continuously exist in eternity according to them while being originated essentially. And it is objected to it that the non-necessitation of existence, even if it is a state established for the contingent by its essence, does not necessitate its necessitation of non-existence, so that its non-existence would be prior to its existence by essential priority, as they claimed. Yes, the non-necessitation of existence and non-existence because it is based on the essence of the contingent is prior to the necessitation of existence because it is based on another. Then if one makes the priority of the deservingness of existence over non-deservingness of it [the definition of] essential origination, as Imam al-Razi did, it is correct.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage discusses an objection to the philosophers' proof and offers Imam al-Razi's alternative. First, the commentator notes that the philosophers' definition of essential origination makes it similar to temporal origination in that existence is preceded by non-existence, but with essential priority instead of temporal. Some scholars explicitly state this, but it is problematic because non-existence cannot be essentially prior to existence; if it were, it would be a cause or part of a cause of existence, which is absurd for eternally existing contingent beings (like the celestial spheres in their view). The objection then directly targets the proof: the fact that a contingent does not necessitate existence by itself does not imply that it necessitates non-existence; therefore, non-existence is not essentially prior. However, it is correct that the state of 'not necessitating existence or non-existence' (i.e., pure potentiality) is prior to 'necessitating existence' from a cause. Therefore, if one defines essential origination as the priority of the state of 'not deserving existence' over 'deserving existence' (i.e., being needful of a cause), as Imam al-Razi did, then the definition stands without the problematic implication.

Key Terms
مسبوقية الوجود بالعدم
استحقاق الوجود
العدم
الإمام الرازي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Essential origination requires non-existence to temporally precede existence.
Correction: Essential origination involves priority by essence, not time, and Imam al-Razi shows it is really about the priority of the state of being needful over receiving existence.

Checkpoint
What is the main objection to the philosophers' proof for essential origination?
A) Non-existence cannot be essentially prior to existence because that would make non-existence a cause of existence.
B) The proof confuses temporal priority with essential priority.
C) Contingent beings do not need a cause.
D) Essential origination applies only to material things.

Key Takeaway
Essential origination is correctly defined as the priority of the state of not deserving existence over deserving it, not as non-existence preceding existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your existence is not just temporally but essentially dependent on Allah every moment, how would that change the way you live your day? What one habit would you change to remind yourself of this dependence?
?
The philosophers thought that even eternal beings are essentially originated. Do you ever feel that your own good qualities or successes are 'self-made'? How can you actively attribute them to Allah's causation, not just at the start but continuously?
?
Imam al-Razi refined the definition to avoid making non-existence a cause. In your life, do you sometimes treat absence or lack as a cause for your actions? What would it mean to instead see your actions as stemming from a lack of deservingness and Allah's gift?

The Claim of Essential Priority and Its Objection
The initial argument and the objection to it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that the possible's non-necessitation of existence is essentially prior to its necessitation by another, and the objection that this does not entail the priority of non-existence.

Core Idea
Non-necessitation does not automatically mean non-existence is prior.

This passage presents a key argument in the theology of origination: that the possible's lack of inherent necessitation of existence is prior to its being made to exist by an external cause. However, the objection clarifies that non-necessitation is about indifference, not a positive claim about non-existence. Let's examine the argument and the subtle refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
The passage starts by stating that the possible's essence is prior to its existence, otherwise it would be a cause. Note the context of continuants in pre-eternity.
2
Read the objection
The objection states that non-necessitation does not necessitate priority of non-existence. Understand the distinction between non-necessitation and a positive act of necessitating non-existence.
3
Consider the implication
Reflect on why the objectors think the argument fails. This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد السادس : أبحاث الحدوث
تقدم له بالذات على الوجود، وإلا لكان علة له أوجزءاً لعلته، ولا يتصور ذلك في الممكنات المستمرة الوجود في الأزل عندهم مع كونها محدثة حدوثاً ذاتياً. (ويرد عليه) أي على الدليل الذي ذكروه أن عدم اقتضاء الوجود وإن كان أمراً ثابتاً للممكن بحسب ذاته، لكنه لا يوجب اقتضاءه أي اقتضاء الممكن لذاته العدم، فيكون عدمه سابقاً على وجوده سبقاً ذاتياً، كما زعموه. نعم لا اقتضاء الوجود والعدم؛ لكونه مستنداً إلى ذات الممكن سابق على اقتضاء الوجود لكونه مستنداً إلى غيره، فإن جعل مسبوقية استحقاق الوجود بلا استحقاقيته حدوثاً ذاتياً، كما فعله الإمام الرازي صح، إن ثبت أن ما بالذات مقدم بالذات على ما بالغير، لكنه منظور فيه؛ لأن غاية ما ذكروه في إثباته أن ارتفاع الأول يستلزم ارتفاع الثاني، من دون عكس. وليس يلزم منه تقدم الأول على الثاني إلا إذا ثبت أن ارتفاعه سبب لارتفاعه، ولم [؟] لوجوده مقدم على وجوده وفيه أنه مع كونه خلاف الظاهر مستدرك بعد بيان أن علة الحاجة إلى المؤثر هو الإمكان، وأنه حينئذ يكون راجعاً إلى ما قاله الإمام، والكلام في أن القول بالتقدم الذاتي للعدم مشكل، ومن هذا ظهر بطلان ما قيل إن المراد أن إمكان عدمه متقدم على وجوده مع أن التخصيص بإمكان العدم لا معنى له، لأن الإمكان مطلقاً مقدم على وجوده. ولو سلم فكما أن إمكان عدمه مقدم على وجوده يصح أن يقال: إن إمكان وجوده مقدم على وجوده، بل نقول: إمكان كل ظرف مقدم على وجوده، لا إمكان ظرف آخر.
The Third Observatory - The Sixth Objective: Investigations of Origination. Its priority by essence over existence, otherwise it would be a cause for it or a part of its cause, and that is not conceivable in the continuously existing possibles in pre-eternity according to them while they are originated by essential origination. (And it is objected) i.e., to the proof they mentioned that the non-necessitation of existence, although it is a matter established for the possible according to its essence, yet it does not necessitate its necessitation, i.e., the possible's necessitation of non-existence for itself, so that its non-existence would be prior to its existence by essential priority, as they claimed. Indeed, the non-necessitation of existence and non-existence, because it is dependent on the essence of the possible, is prior to the necessitation of existence because it is dependent on another. For if making the priority of entitlement to existence over its non-entitlement an essential origination, as Imam al-Razi did, is correct, provided it is established that what is by essence is essentially prior to what is by another, but it is subject to scrutiny; because the extent of what they mentioned in proving it is that the removal of the first necessitates the removal of the second, without the converse. And from that does not necessarily follow the priority of the first over the second unless it is established that its removal is the cause of its removal, and not [?] its existence is prior to its existence. And in it, while it is contrary to the apparent, it is redundant after the clarification that the cause of the need for the cause (al-mu'aththir) is possibility (al-imkan), and that then it would refer back to what Imam said. And the discussion is that the claim of essential priority of non-existence is problematic. And from this appears the invalidity of what was said that what is meant is that the possibility of its non-existence is prior to its existence, while the specification by possibility of non-existence has no meaning, because possibility absolutely is prior to its existence. And if it is granted, then just as the possibility of its non-existence is prior to its existence, it is valid to say that the possibility of its existence is prior to its existence. Rather, we say: the possibility of every aspect is prior to its existence, not the possibility of another aspect.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument concerning the claim that the possible's non-necessitation of existence is essentially prior to its necessitation by another, which is used to define essential origination. The passage begins by stating that the priority of the possible's essence over its existence is such that if it were not prior, it would either be a cause or part of a cause, which is not conceivable for continuously existing possibles in pre-eternity according to the theologians who hold them to be originated by essential origination. Then it presents an objection: The fact that the possible does not necessitate existence (lack of necessitation) is an attribute of its essence, but this does not entail that it necessitates its own non-existence (a different claim). So the claim that non-existence is essentially prior to existence is not justified by mere non-necessitation. The passage then clarifies that the non-necessitation of both existence and non-existence (the state of indifference) is prior to the necessitation of existence (which comes from an external cause). If one makes the precedence of entitlement to existence over non-entitlement the criterion for essential origination, as Imam al-Razi did, that would be correct provided it is proven that 'what is by essence' is essentially prior to 'what is by another'. However, this is questionable because the proof they offer (that elimination of the first entails elimination of the second but not vice versa) does not imply priority unless it is shown that the elimination of the first is the cause of the elimination of the second. The passage then notes that this line of argument is problematic and ultimately reduces to the Imam's position. It concludes by showing the invalidity of the claim that the possibility of non-existence is prior to existence, since possibility as such is prior to existence, not specifically the possibility of non-existence. Hence, the correct view is that the possibility of every aspect (both existence and non-existence) is prior to its existence.

Key Terms
حدوث
اقتضاء
بالذات
بالغير
ذاتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Non-necessitation of existence means the possible essentially requires non-existence.
Correction: Non-necessitation means indifference; it does not entail necessitation of non-existence.

Checkpoint
What is the objection to the claim that non-necessitation of existence is essentially prior to existence?
A) Non-necessitation is not an attribute of the essence.
B) Non-necessitation does not entail that the possible necessitates its own non-existence.
C) The possible always necessitates its own existence.
D) The possible cannot be prior to anything.

Key Takeaway
Non-necessitation of existence is an inherent property of the possible, but it does not imply that non-existence is essentially prior.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you assume that because something is not guaranteed, it must be absent? How does this lesson challenge that assumption?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you ever feel that non-existence is more natural than existence? How does the objection in this passage correct that feeling?
?
This lesson shows that non-necessitation does not imply necessity of non-existence. How does this affect your gratitude for the existence that Allah has granted you?

Examining the Proof of Essential Priority and the Role of Possibility
The critique of the proof and the final clarification about possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the critique of the proof that what is by essence is prior to what is by another, and the final conclusion that possibility as such is prior to existence.

Core Idea
Possibility, not just possibility of non-existence, is prior to existence.

After the objection, the passage delves into a deeper analysis. It discusses the conditions for essential priority and critiques the common proof. The resolution clarifies that the priority belongs to possibility in general, not specifically to the possibility of non-existence. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the alternative formulation
The passage presents Imam al-Razi's view that the priority of non-entitlement to existence over entitlement can be considered essential origination, if a certain condition holds.
2
Examine the proof's weakness
The proof that removal of first entails removal of second does not establish priority unless the removal is the cause. Consider why this is insufficient.
3
Trace the conclusion about possibility
The passage concludes that the possibility of every aspect (both existence and non-existence) is prior to existence, not just one aspect.

The passage then clarifies that the non-necessitation of both existence and non-existence (the state of indifference) is prior to the necessitation of existence (which comes from an external cause). If one makes the precedence of entitlement to existence over non-entitlement the criterion for essential origination, as Imam al-Razi did, that would be correct provided it is proven that 'what is by essence' is essentially prior to 'what is by another'. However, this is questionable because the proof they offer (that elimination of the first entails elimination of the second but not vice versa) does not imply priority unless it is shown that the elimination of the first is the cause of the elimination of the second. The passage then notes that this line of argument is problematic and ultimately reduces to the Imam's position. It concludes by showing the invalidity of the claim that the possibility of non-existence is prior to existence, since possibility as such is prior to existence, not specifically the possibility of non-existence. Hence, the correct view is that the possibility of every aspect (both existence and non-existence) is prior to its existence.

Key Terms
إمكان
استحقاق
ذاتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only the possibility of non-existence is prior to existence.
Correction: Possibility as such (both of existence and non-existence) is prior to existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the problem with the claim that the possibility of non-existence is prior to existence?
A) Possibility of non-existence is not real.
B) Possibility of existence is also prior, and specifying one aspect is meaningless.
C) Possibility is posterior to existence.
D) The possible does not have possibility of non-existence.

Key Takeaway
The priority belongs to possibility in general, not to a specific possibility of non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that possibility in general is prior to existence. Do you habitually focus on only one outcome (like failure) while ignoring the broader reality that all possibilities are from Allah? How will you train yourself to see every possibility as equally prior and equally within His control?
?
Imam al-Razi had a specific argument for priority that was refined. Are you willing to have your own deeply held beliefs about Allah and existence examined and corrected, even if it is uncomfortable? Will you seek out knowledge that challenges your assumptions, or do you prefer to remain comfortable?

Proof that Possibility Requires a Locus and Is Not the Possible Thing Itself
Proof that possibility requires a locus and refutation that the locus is the possible thing itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why possibility (imkan) must subsist in a locus and why that locus cannot be the possible thing itself.

Core Idea
Possibility cannot stand alone; it needs a locus, and that locus cannot be the possible thing itself.

This passage presents a foundational argument in kalam: the attribute of possibility must inhere in a subject. But then a critical question arises: could that subject be the possible thing itself? The proof shows this is impossible because it would require the thing to precede itself, which is self-contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the argument's flow come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage includes both main text and commentary.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the statement that possibility requires a locus. What reason is given?
The reason is that possibility cannot subsist by itself.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage argues that the locus cannot be the possible thing itself. Why? Because the possible thing does not exist before its existence.
This uses the premise that a thing cannot precede itself.
4
Analyze the objection and response
Some might say that after establishing that possibility exists before the existent, there is no need to negate the locus being the thing itself. The commentator refutes this.
The response distinguishes between mental impossibility and actual impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يستدعي محلاً؛ لامتناع قيام الإمكان بنفسه؛ (موجوداً) إذ يستحيل قيام الصفة الوجودية بالمعدوم، وليس ذلك المحل نفسه) أي نفس ذلك الحادث الممكن، إذ لا يوجد قبل وجوده)، فكيف يتصور كونه نفس ذلك المحل الموجود قبله حتى يقوم به إمكانه. قوله: ( لامتناع قيام الإمكان إلخ) لكونه أمراً إضافياً. قوله: ( وليس ذلك المحل نفسه بعد إثبات أن الحادث قبل وجوده ممكن، وأن الإمكان محلاً موجوداً، أثبت أن محله ليس نفس الحادث بضم مقدمة ثالثة بديهية، وهو امتناع تقدم الشيء على نفسه المفاد بقوله : إذ لا يوجد قبل وجوده فما قيل من أنه بعد تحقيق أن الإمكان موجود قبل وجود الحادث لا حاجة إلى نفي كون محله نفس ذلك الحادث وهو ظاهر، ولا يحتمل هذا حتى ينفي، وخصوصاً قد نفاه بهذا التحقيق ليس بشيء؛ لأنه إن أراد عدم الاحتمال عند العقل فممنوع، وإن أراد في نفس الأمر فلا يجدي ولأنه ما نفاه بهذا التحقيق، بل بضم مقدمة أخرى بديهية. لظهوره .
(It [i.e., the occuring thing before its existence] requires a locus; because it is impossible for possibility to subsist by itself; (existent) since it is impossible for an existent attribute to subsist in a non-existent, and that locus is not itself) meaning the possible occuring thing itself, since it does not exist before its existence), so how can it be imagined that it is itself that locus that exists before it so that its possibility subsists in it? His saying: (because it is impossible for the possibility to subsist etc.) because it is a relational matter. His saying: (and that locus is not itself) after establishing that the occuring thing before its existence is possible, and that possibility exists, he established that its locus is not the occuring thing itself by adding a third self-evident premise, namely the impossibility of a thing preceding itself, expressed by his saying: 'since it does not exist before its existence.' So what is said, that after establishing that possibility exists before the existence of the occuring thing there is no need to negate that its locus is that same occuring thing, and this is obvious, and does not require this negation, especially since he negated it by this establishment, is nothing; because if he intends improbability in the mind, it is denied, and if he intends in reality it does not avail, and because he did not negate it by this establishment, but rather by adding another self-evident premise. Because of its obviousness.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a proof that possibility (imkan) requires a locus (mahall) and that this locus cannot be the possible thing itself. The main text argues: every occuring thing (al-hadith) before its existence is possible; possibility is an existent attribute; it cannot subsist by itself; therefore it needs a locus. This locus cannot be the possible thing itself because the possible thing does not exist before its existence, and to say that the locus is itself would require a thing to precede itself, which is impossible. The commentator clarifies that possibility is relational (amr idafi), and that the argument uses a third self-evident premise (badihiyya): the impossibility of a thing preceding itself. He refutes a possible objection: some might say that after establishing that possibility exists before the occuring thing, there is no need to negate that its locus is the occuring thing itself. The commentator responds that this objection is invalid because the impossibility in the mind is not impossible, and in reality it does not help; the negation is proven by the self-evident premise of the impossibility of self-precedence.

Key Terms
الإمكان
المحل
الحادث
الصفة الوجودية
المعدوم
الأمر الإضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the locus of possibility could be the possible thing itself, because possibility is an attribute that inheres in the thing when it exists.
Correction: This is impossible because before existence, the possible thing does not exist, so it cannot be a locus for its own possibility. The locus must be something else that exists prior to the thing.

Checkpoint
What is the self-evident premise used to prove that the locus of possibility cannot be the possible thing itself?
A) The impossibility of a thing preceding itself.
B) The impossibility of an accident subsisting by itself.
C) The necessity of a substrate for every attribute.
D) The impossibility of the existence of two possibilities.

Key Takeaway
Possibility is an attribute that must inhere in an existent locus, and this locus cannot be the possible thing itself without violating the principle of non-contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your entire existence—every talent, every breath—is held by a possibility that cannot reside in you, then who holds your reality? How often do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What would change if you truly believed that your very possibility depends on something outside yourself?
?
The proof shows that a thing cannot be the foundation of its own possibility. In what areas of your life are you trying to be your own foundation, ignoring that you depend entirely on Allah for your existence and sustenance? What step will you take today to acknowledge that dependence actively?
?
You have seen that the impossiblity of self-precedence is a clear logical barrier. Yet in your daily choices, do you not often act as if you can precede Allah's will—planning your future without reference to His decree? How can you align your actions with the truth that your own possibility does not reside in you?

Why the Locus of Possibility Is Not Separate
The author argues that the locus of possibility is not completely separate nor a separate but related entity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the locus of possibility cannot be something completely separate nor something separate in existence, and how the example of power clarifies this.

Core Idea
The locus of possibility is neither a disconnected entity nor a separate attribute—only a unified essence can bear possibilities.

In the previous lesson, we established that the locus of possibility must be posited. But what kind of thing is it? The author now eliminates two mistaken views: that it is something completely external to the occuring thing, or that it is something related to it yet existentially separate. This passage refines our understanding by drawing on the principle that attributes cannot subsist in what is separate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the two negations: 'not separate' and 'nor related but distinct'.
2
Identify the two rejected views
The passage refutes two possibilities: (1) the locus is completely separate (munfasil) with no connection, and (2) it is related but separate in existence (mubayin). Find these in the text.
The first is dismissed as obviously unsuitable; the second requires a more subtle argument.
3
Understand the reasoning for each rejection
For the first: a completely separate thing cannot be a locus at all. For the second: an attribute cannot subsist in something separate from its subject. The text gives the example of the power of the agent (qudrat al-qadir) as a case of something separate.
The key principle: 'the attribute of a thing does not subsist in what is separate from it.'
4
Examine the commentator's clarification
The commentator explains that 'separate in existence' does not mean two independent existences, but the absence of correlation (muqarana) between them in reality.
This prevents a possible misinterpretation: the negation is about existential correlation, not numerical distinctness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا) أمراً (منفصلاً) الحادث بالكلية، لا تعلق له به أصلاً فإنه لا يصلح أن يكون محلاً لإمكانه قطعاً، ولا أمراً متعلقاً به إذا كان ومبايناً له في الوجود ؛ لأن صفة الشيء لا تقوم بما يباينه، (كقدرة القادر منفصلاً عنه، قوله : ( ولا أمراً متعلقاً به إلخ) أشار بالتعميم إلى أن الاحتمال الأول متروك بيانه في المتن قوله : ( ومبايناً له في الوجود) ليس المراد به نفي أن يكون لكل منهما وجود على حدة، بل نفي المقارنة بينهما في التحقيق، كما سيجيء.
(Nor) is it a thing (completely separate) from the occuring thing, having no connection to it at all, for it would not be suitable as a locus for its possibility at all, nor is it a thing related to it while being separate from it in existence; because the attribute of a thing does not subsist in what is separate from it, (like the power of the powerful being separate from him). His saying: (and nor a thing related to it etc.) He indicated by the generalization that the first possibility is left to be explained in the text. His saying: (and separate from it in existence) what is meant by it is not the negation that each has an existence on its own, but rather the negation of correlation between them in reality, as will come.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage completes the proof by refuting two remaining possibilities for the locus of possibility: it cannot be something completely separate (munfasil) from the occuring thing, with no connection at all, because such an unrelated thing cannot serve as a locus. Nor can it be something that is related to the occuring thing but is existentially separate (mubayin), because an attribute cannot subsist in a separate entity. The example given is the power of the agent (qudrat al-qadir) which is separate from the agent but still relates to it? Actually, the example is given as a case where the attribute (power) is separate from the agent? The commentator clarifies that 'separate in existence' does not mean that each has its own existence independently, but rather that there is no correlation (muqarana) between them in reality. This is a key point: the negation is about existential correlation, not numerical distinctness.

قدرة القادر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'separate in existence' means two entities that have their own independent existences.
Correction: The commentator clarifies: it means absence of correlation (muqarana) in reality, not that each has a separate existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot the locus of possibility be something that is related to the occuring thing but separate in existence?
A) Because a locus must be completely unconnected.
B) Because an attribute cannot subsist in something separate from its subject.
C) Because the occuring thing would be impossible without it.
D) Because the power of the agent is separate from him.

Key Takeaway
The locus of possibility cannot be either completely separate or existentially separate; it must be intimately connected with the occuring thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself acting as if your potential or ability is separate from who you are, as if success or failure depends on something external rather than your own essence? How does the principle that possibility subsists in the essence itself challenge the way you approach your own growth?
?
If the locus of possibility cannot be separate, then your very existence and potentialities are not independent of the Creator's sustaining power. In what specific area of your life are you living as if you are self-sufficient, and what would it mean to truly internalize that your possibility of being is inseparable from Him?

The Substrate of Possibility: Three Rejected Candidates
Al-Jurjani enumerates and rejects three possible substrates for possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why possibility requires a substrate and how al-Jurjani rejects three possible substrates for the possibility of a temporal entity.

Core Idea
Possibility needs a home, and it cannot be the possible thing itself.

Al-Jurjani begins a crucial inquiry in metaphysics: where does the attribute of 'possibility' reside? Since possibility is an attribute, it requires a substrate—an existent thing in which it inheres. But the possible entity is not yet existent before its occurrence. So what bears its possibility? In this passage, al-Jurjani systematically rejects three candidates for this substrate, tightening the argument toward the correct view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the flow of arguments as al-Jurjani lists three rejected candidates.
The passage is dense; read slowly and note the key terms.
2
Identify the three rejected substrates
List the three candidates that al-Jurjani considers as possible substrates for possibility. Understand why each is rejected based on the text.
The candidates are: the possible entity itself, something completely separate, and something related but separate.
3
Understand the logic behind each rejection
For each candidate, al-Jurjani provides a specific reason. Grasp the logic: the first is impossible because it would entail self-precedence; the second because the substrate must have a connection; the third because an attribute cannot inhere in a separate entity.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument is foundational in kalam. If possibility had no substrate, then temporal entities could not be rationally grounded before they exist.
This leads to the conclusion that possibility inheres in a pre-eternal substrate, namely the divine essence or the knowledge of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوده في بابه، يستدعي محلاً؛ لامتناع قيام الإمكان بنفسه؛ موجوداً إذ يستحيل قيام الصفة الوجودية بالمعدوم، وليس ذلك المحل نفسه أي نفس ذلك الحادث الممكن، إذ لا يوجد قبل وجوده، فكيف يتصور كونه نفس ذلك المحل الموجود قبله حتى يقوم به إمكانه، ولا أمراً منفصلاً عن الحادث بالكلية، لا تعلق له به أصلاً فإنه لا يصلح أن يكون محلاً لإمكانه قطعاً، ولا أمراً متعلقاً به إذا كان ومبايناً له في الوجود؛ لأن صفة الشيء لا تقوم بما يباينه. قوله : ( لامتناع قيام الإمكان إلخ) لكونه أمراً إضافياً. قوله : ( وليس ذلك المحل نفسه بعد إثبات أن الحادث قبل وجوده ممكن، وأن الإمكان محلاً موجوداً ، أثبت أن محله ليس نفس الحادث بضم مقدمة ثالثة بديهية، وهو امتناع تقدم الشيء على نفسه المفاد بقوله : إذ لا يوجد قبل وجوده
Its existence in its section requires a substrate; because possibility cannot subsist by itself; (it is) existent because the attribution of an existential attribute to the non-existent is impossible, and that substrate is not itself – i.e., that same temporal possible, since it does not exist before its existence – so how can it be conceived as being that same substrate existing before it so that its possibility subsists in it? Nor (is it) a thing completely separate from the temporal, having no connection to it at all, for it is absolutely not suitable to be a substrate for its possibility. Nor (is it) a thing related to it if it is separate from it in existence, because an attribute of a thing does not subsist in what is separate from it. His statement: (regarding the impossibility of possibility subsisting by itself etc.) because it is a relational matter. His statement: (and that substrate is not itself) after establishing that the temporal before its existence is possible, and that possibility is existent in a substrate, he proved that its substrate is not the temporal itself by adding a third evident premise, which is the impossibility of a thing preceding itself, conveyed by his statement: 'since it does not exist before its existence'.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage defines the argument for the substrate of possibility. It begins by stating that possibility, as an attribute, cannot subsist by itself; it requires a substrate because it is an existential attribute, and an existential attribute cannot inhere in a non-existent. The author then examines three candidates for the substrate: 1) the possible entity itself, 2) something completely separate, and 3) something related but separate. The first is rejected because the possible entity does not exist before its own existence, so it cannot be the substrate for its possibility that precedes existence. The second is rejected because something completely separate cannot bear the attribute of the possible. The third candidate, something related but separate, is also rejected on the grounds that an attribute of a thing cannot reside in something separate from it. The commentary adds that the impossibility of possibility subsisting by itself is because it is a relational (i‘tibārī) matter, and that the proof that the substrate is not the possible entity itself relies on a third evident premise: the impossibility of a thing preceding itself, which is clear from the fact that the possible does not exist before its existence.

Key Terms

محل
الصفة الوجودية
المعدوم
المباينة
أمر إضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that possibility can subsist in the possible entity itself even before it exists.
Correction: The text explicitly argues that this is impossible because the possible entity does not exist before its existence, so it cannot be a substrate for its own possibility.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why cannot the substrate of possibility be the possible entity itself?
A) Because possibility is a non-relational attribute.
B) Because the possible entity does not exist before its own existence.
C) Because the possible entity is separate from its possibility.
D) Because possibility is not an existential attribute.

Key Takeaway
Possibility cannot subsist without an existent substrate, and the possible entity itself cannot bear its own possibility before existence.
